## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a population (dP/dt) as a function of time and current population size. Classical population dynamics models express growth rates through various density-dependent and density-independent mechanisms, ranging from simple exponential growth to complex models with Allee effects and seasonal forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth decelerating logarithmically near carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with flexible inflection point)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below critical threshold)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 - c2 * P) (per-capita growth rate increases then decreases with density)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with density-proportional removal)
- Logistic with constant harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (growth with constant removal rate)
- Von Bertalanffy growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - c3 * P) (logistic growth with periodic environmental forcing)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Exponential decay toward carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (growth suppressed exponentially at high density)
- Beverton-Holt continuous analog: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent birth with linear death)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P (dP_dt ~ c*P) indicates density-independent per-capita growth rate, characteristic of exponential/Malthusian dynamics
- Quadratic terms in P (dP_dt containing P² term) indicate intraspecific competition or density-dependent regulation as in logistic models
- Cubic terms in P (dP_dt containing P³ or P²(1-cP) structure) suggest Allee effects where very small populations have negative growth
- Logarithmic dependence on P (log(P) terms) suggests Gompertz-type growth where per-capita rate declines logarithmically with population
- Explicit time dependence through trigonometric functions of t indicates seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on growth parameters
- Ratio forms P/(1+cP) indicate saturating functional responses where per-capita resource availability decreases with crowding
- Constant additive terms (independent of P) represent immigration, stocking, or constant-rate harvesting pressures
- Product of multiple factors involving P (e.g., P*(P-a)*(K-P)) indicates multiple ecological thresholds governing population behavior
- Exponential functions of P (exp(-cP)) represent strong density-dependent inhibition that acts more sharply than polynomial suppression
- Fractional powers of P (P^c where 0<c<1) indicate sublinear scaling often associated with surface-area-to-volume metabolic constraints

with \(A=0.3156057016002752\), \(k=0.05405074842498068\), \(B=9.870854086995406\).
Key structural facts:
- The only \(t\)-dependence is through a single exponential \(e^{-kt}\) multiplied by \(P\). No sines/cosines/logs/polynomials in \(t\).
- The remaining term is a rational function of \(P\) only: \(A P^2/(BP+1)\).
- There is **no** standalone constant term, no standalone \(P\) term without the \(e^{-kt}\) factor, and no \(\log\) terms.

Now check candidates (can set candidate constants freely, including to 0):

1) \(P c0 + P^{c1}c2\cos(c3 t)+ c4\log(Pc5+1)+c6\).  
To match GT, must remove cos/log/constant: set \(c2=0,c4=0,c6=0\). Left with \(Pc0\), but GT is not purely linear in \(P\) and has \(t\)-dependence. No.

2) Linear-in-\(P\) sum + \(\log(Pc5+c6 t+1)\) + \(\exp(Pc8+c9 t)\).  
To avoid wrong \(t\) forms, would need kill log and exp terms; then only linear/constant remains. Cannot produce \(P e^{-kt}\) plus \(P^2/(BP+1)\). No.

3) \(Pc0 + c1\log(c2 t+1)+ c3 e^{c4 t}+ c5 e^{c6\sin(\cdot)}\).  
GT needs \(P e^{-kt}\) (a \(t\)-exponential multiplied by \(P\)), but here the \(t\)-exponential is not multiplied by \(P\). Also has log/sin-exp unless zeroed; zeroing leaves \(Pc0\). No.

4) \(Pc0 + \frac{P c1}{P c2+1}+ c3\log(Pc4+1)+ c5\sin(\cdot)+ c8 t + c9\).  
Can set \(c3=c5=c8=c9=0\). Then \(Pc0 + \frac{P c1}{P c2+1}\), which is \(P\) times a rational in \(P\), not \(P e^{-kt}\) plus \(P^2/(BP+1)\). Also no \(t\)-dependence remains. No.

Can kill log/sin: \(c4=0,c7=0\). Then \(Pc0 + c2 P^{c1} e^{c3 t}\). This gives a separable term \(P^{c1}e^{c3 t}\) plus a linear \(P\) term. GT needs \(P e^{-kt}\) plus a **rational** \(P^2/(BP+1)\). No way to get the rational term. No.

7) \(Pc0 + c1\log(Pc2+c3 t+1)+ c4 e^{c5 t}+ c6 e^{c7\sin(\cdot)}\).

9) \(Pc0+Pc1 + \sin(\cdot)+ \log(P\cdot)+ \log(t\cdot)+c9\).

10) \(Pc0 + c1\log(Pc2+c3 t+1)+ c4\log(Pc5+1)\cos(c6 t)+ c7/P^4\).

18) Big expression all over \((P c1+1)\) with logs.  
Even if logs removed, it becomes a sum of terms like \(P^2/(P c1+1)\) and \(P/(P c1+1)\), but **still no \(t\)-dependent \(P e^{-kt}\)** term. Also GT’s rational term is \(P^2/(BP+1)\) times \(A\) with no extra \(P/(BP+1)\) pieces unless forced to zero—yet even then missing the exponential-in-\(t\) part. No.

19) \(Pc0 + \frac{P}{P c1+1}+ c2\log(Pc3+1)+ c4 e^{c5\cos(c6 t)}\).  
Zero log/exp gives \(Pc0 + \frac{P}{P c1+1}\), no \(t\). No.

To match GT, must remove log/cos/\(P^{-4}\). Remaining \(Pc0 + c6 e^{c7 t}\) (no \(P\) factor on exponential, and no rational \(P\)-term). No.

Cannot create \(P e^{-kt}\) or \(P^2/(BP+1)\). Zeroing extras leaves \(Pc0\). No.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG1)
============================================================
GT: c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + c2*P**c3/(c4*P + c5)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: 0.3156*P*exp(-0.05405*t) + 0.3156*P²/(9.871*P + 1)**

The GT has two terms:
1. A term proportional to P*exp(-c₁*t) — an exponential decay in t multiplied by P
2. A rational term P²/(c₄*P + c₅) — a rational function of P only

Let me analyze the structure. The key basis functions are:
- P*exp(αt) where α < 0
- P²/(aP + b) — a rational function in P

Now let me check each candidate systematically.

**Key observations about GT structure:**
- The t-dependence comes ONLY through exp(-0.054*t)
- The P-dependence involves both P*exp(...) and P²/(linear in P)
- P²/(aP+b) can be rewritten as (P/a) - (b/a²)*P/(P + b/a) + ... Actually, let me do polynomial division: P²/(aP+b) = P/a - b/a² + b²/(a²(aP+b))

Let me check if any candidate can match.

For a candidate to match, it needs:
1. A P*exp(αt) term (exponential in t, linear in P)
2. A P²/(linear P) term or equivalent

Let me go through candidates looking for these features:

**Candidate 1:** P*c0 + P^c1*c2*cos(c3*t) + c4*log(P*c5+1) + c6
- cos vs exp: can't match exp(-ct) with cos. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 2:** P*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2 + c3 + c4*log(P*c5+c6*t+1) + c7*exp(P*c8+c9*t)
- Has exp(c9*t) but multiplied by exp(P*c8), not by P. If c8=0, then c7*exp(c9*t) — not multiplied by P. The log term mixes P and t. Can't produce P*exp(αt). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 3:** P*c0 + c1*log(c2*t+1) + c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*exp(c6*sin(c7*t+c8))
- No P² term or P/(P+c) term. The exp(c4*t) isn't multiplied by P. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 4:** P*c0 + P*c1/(P*c2+1) + c3*log(P*c4+1) + c5*sin(c6+c7*t) + c8*t + c9
- Has P*c1/(P*c2+1) which is a rational function of P
- Has sin for t-dependence, not exp. Can set c5=0 and c8=0, but then no exp(-ct) term. **NO MATCH** (missing exp decay)

**Candidate 5:** P*c0 + P^c1*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*log(P*c5+c6*t+1) + c7*sin(c8+c9*t)
- P^c1*c2*exp(c3*t): if c1=1, this gives P*c2*exp(c3*t) ✓ for the first GT term
- Need P²/(aP+1) from remaining terms: P*c0 + c4*log(P*c5+c6*t+1) + c7*sin(...)
- Set c7=0, c6=0: P*c0 + c4*log(P*c5+1)
- P*c0 + c4*log(P*c5+1) ≠ P²/(aP+1). log ≠ rational function. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 6:** Similar to 4 with sin and cos. No exp decay. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 7:** P*c0 + c1*log(P*c2+c3*t+1) + c4*exp(c5*t) + c6*exp(c7*sin(c8*t+c9))
- exp(c5*t) not multiplied by P. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 8:** P*c0 + P*c1/(P*c2+1) + c3*log(P*c4+1) + c5*sin(c6+c7*t)
- No exp term. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 9-50:** Let me scan for candidates that have BOTH P*exp(αt) AND P²/(aP+b) or P/(P+c).

Looking through all candidates, I need:
- A term like P*exp(ct) or P^c1*exp(ct) with c1 settable to 1
- A term like P²/(aP+b) or P*c/(Pc+1)

Note: P*c1/(P*c2+1) can be rewritten as c1/c2 - c1/(c2(P*c2+1)), which is NOT P²/(aP+b).

Actually, P²/(aP+b) = P·P/(aP+b). And P·c1/(P·c2+1) = c1·P/(c2·P+1).

Can P*c0 + P*c1/(P*c2+1) equal P²/(aP+b)?
P*c0 + c1*P/(c2*P+1) = [c0*P*(c2*P+1) + c1*P]/(c2*P+1) = [c0*c2*P² + (c0+c1)*P]/(c2*P+1)

GT's rational part: 0.3156*P²/(9.871*P+1). This has NO linear P term in numerator.

So I need c0+c1=0, i.e., c1=-c0. Then: [c0*c2*P² - c0*P]/(c2*P+1). But GT has 0 coefficient on P in numerator. So c0=0, but then the whole thing is 0. Unless... wait, let me reconsider.

Actually the GT also has the exp term: c0*P*exp(-c1*t). At t=0, this contributes c0*P. So the full GT is:
0.3156*P*exp(-0.054t) + 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1)

For candidates with P*c0 + P*c1/(P*c2+1), the combined rational part:
[c0*c2*P² + (c0+c1)*P]/(c2*P+1)

To match 0.3156*P²/(9.871P+1), need c0+c1=0 and c0*c2=0.3156 with c2=9.871. So c0=0.03197, c1=-0.03197.

But then the exp(-0.054t) term needs to come from somewhere else. These candidates (4, 6, 8, etc.) have sin/cos for t-dependence, not exp.

Let me look more carefully for candidates with BOTH a rational P term AND exp(t):

**Candidate 11:** P*c0/(P*c1+1) + P*c2 + c3*exp(c4*cos(c5*t)) + c6*log(P^c7*c8+1)
- Has P*c0/(Pc1+1) + Pc2 → rational in P ✓
- exp(c4*cos(c5*t)) ≠ P*exp(αt). Not multiplied by P, and cos inside exp. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 12:** P*c0/(P*c1+1) + P*c2 + c3*log(P*c4+1) + c5*exp(c6*cos(c7*t))
- Same issue: exp(c6*cos(c7*t)) not P*exp(αt). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 18:** Complex expression with P²/(Pc1+1) terms and log terms. No exp(t). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 19:** P*c0 + P/(Pc1+1) + c2*log(Pc3+1) + c4*exp(c5*cos(c6*t))
- exp of cos, not exp(αt). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 23:** P*c0 + P + c1*log(P*c2+c3*t+1) + c4*exp(c5*t) + c6*cos(c7*t)
- c4*exp(c5*t) not multiplied by P. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 24:** P*c0 + c1*log(P*c2+c3*t+1) + c4*exp(c5*t) + c6 + c7*cos(c8*t)
- exp not multiplied by P. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 28:** P*c0 + P*c1 + c2*log(P*c3+c4*t+1) + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*cos(c8*t)
- exp not multiplied by P. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 31:** P*c0 + c1*log(P*c2+c3*t+1) + c4*exp(c5*t) + c6*cos(c7*t)
- exp not multiplied by P. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 36:** P*c0 + P*c1*exp(P*c2) + P^c3*c4*cos(c5*t+c6) + c7*log(P*c8+1) + c9
- P*c1*exp(Pc2): if c2=0, gives Pc1 (constant×P)
- P^c3*c4*cos(c5*t+c6): if c3=1, gives P*c4*cos(c5*t+c6). cos ≠ exp. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 38:** P*c0 + P*c1 + c2*t + c3*log(P*c4+c5*t+1) + c6*exp(c7*t)
- exp not multiplied by P. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 41:** P*c0 + c1*sin(c2*t+c3) + c4*t^c5 + c6 + c7*exp(c8*t)*log(P*c9+1)
- c7*exp(c8*t)*log(P*c9+1): log(P*c9+1) ≈ c9*P for small c9*P, but not exact. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 44:** P*c0 + P*c1*log(1+c2/P) + c3*log(P*c4+1) + c5*t^c6 + c7
- P*c1*log(1+c2/P): For P>0, log(1+c2/P) is not linear in P. This is interesting but can't produce exp(-αt). Also no t-exponential. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 47:** P*c0 + P*c1 + c2*log(P*c3+c4*t+1) + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*cos(t)
- exp not multiplied by P. **NO MATCH**

After exhaustive search, **none** of the candidates have the required P*exp(αt) term combined with a P²/(aP+b) rational term.

Let me double-check Candidate 5 more carefully:
P*c0 + P^c1*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*log(P*c5+c6*t+1) + c7*sin(c8+c9*t)

log is not a rational function. **NO MATCH**
